11/07/25, 2:46 pm - Dhruv: Thanks, Dhruv! You're comparing:

1. ✅ Acer Aspire 5 AL15-52H – i5-12450H (12th Gen), 16GB RAM, 512GB SSD


2. ✅ ASUS ExpertBook P1 – i5-13420H (13th Gen), 16GB RAM, 512GB SSD



Let’s compare them head-to-head across performance, display, build, battery, and overall value.


---

⚙️ 1. CPU Performance

Feature	i5-12450H (Acer)	i5-13420H (ASUS)

Cores/Threads	8 (4P + 4E) / 12	8 (4P + 4E) / 12
Base / Turbo Clock	~2.0 GHz / 4.4 GHz	~2.1 GHz / 4.6 GHz
Performance Boost	—	~5–7% faster (minor)


Winner: 🟩 ASUS ExpertBook P1

> Slight CPU advantage due to newer generation and higher turbo frequency — but it's a small difference in real-world student use (coding, browsing, MS Office, etc.).




---

💻 2. Display Quality

Feature	Acer Aspire 5	ASUS ExpertBook P1

Size	15.6" FHD IPS (confirmed)	15.6" FHD (usually TN)
Panel Type	✅ IPS – better viewing	❌ TN – narrow angles
Brightness	~250 nits	~220–250 nits


Winner: 🟩 Acer Aspire 5

> IPS panel is significantly better for color, viewing angles, and eye comfort. ASUS often ships with cheaper TN panels in this series.




---

🔋 3. Battery Life

Feature	Acer Aspire 5	ASUS ExpertBook P1

Battery Life	~6–6.5 hours	~5–5.5 hours
Efficiency	Good (cooling helps)	Average


Winner: 🟩 Acer Aspire 5

> Slightly better power management and cooling = longer battery life in real-world use.




---

🧱 4. Build Quality & Design

Feature	Acer Aspire 5	ASUS ExpertBook P1

Chassis	Metal top + plastic base	All plastic
Keyboard	Good, some variants backlit	Average typing feel
Weight	~1.7 kg	~1.7–1.8 kg


Winner: 🟩 Acer Aspire 5

> Feels more premium, more rigid chassis. ASUS ExpertBook P1 has a more “budget build.”




---

🔌 5. Ports & Upgradeability

Both laptops offer:

HDMI

USB-A & USB-C (check if USB-C supports charging)

Upgradeable RAM and SSD


Winner: Tie

> Both are good in this area for student use.




---

🧠 Summary Table

Feature	Winner	Notes

CPU Performance	ASUS P1	Slight edge (not huge)
Display	✅ Acer	IPS vs TN – big difference
Battery	✅ Acer	Slightly better life
Build Quality	✅ Acer	Feels more premium
Portability	Tie	Similar weight
Value for Money	✅ Acer	More features per rupee spent



---

🏆 Final Verdict:

✅ Choose Acer Aspire 5 AL15-52H if:

You care about display quality (IPS) — especially for long hours of reading or coding.

You want better battery, stronger build, and a more balanced laptop.

You're okay with 12th Gen CPU that is still very capable.


✅ Choose ASUS ExpertBook P1 only if:

You get a great deal (lower price), and

You don’t mind a TN panel and all-plastic build,

You want slightly better raw CPU power — for heavy multitasking.



---

> 🎓 For students, especially for coding, online classes, content consumption, and typing — Acer Aspire 5 is the more well-rounded and comfortable laptop to use daily.

20/08/25, 2:09 pm - Dhruv: #include <SPI.h>
#include <MFRC522.h>

#define RST_PIN         9
#define SS_PIN          10
#define GREEN_LED_PIN   7
#define RED_LED_PIN     6

MFRC522 rfid(SS_PIN, RST_PIN);

// Authorized UID
byte authorizedUIDs[][4] = {
  {0x33, 0x5E, 0xF0, 0x20}  // Only this UID will be accepted
};

const int totalAuthorizedCards = sizeof(authorizedUIDs) / sizeof(authorizedUIDs[0]);
bool cardPresent = false;

void setup() {
  Serial.begin(9600);
  SPI.begin();
  rfid.PCD_Init();

  pinMode(GREEN_LED_PIN, OUTPUT);
  pinMode(RED_LED_PIN, OUTPUT);

  digitalWrite(GREEN_LED_PIN, LOW);
  digitalWrite(RED_LED_PIN, LOW);

  Serial.println("Scan your RFID card...");
}

void loop() {
  if (!rfid.PICC_IsNewCardPresent() || !rfid.PICC_ReadCardSerial()) {
    cardPresent = false;
    return;
  }

  if (!cardPresent) {
    if (isAuthorizedCard(rfid.uid.uidByte, rfid.uid.size)) {
      Serial.println("✅ Access Granted!");
      blinkLED(GREEN_LED_PIN);
    } else {
      Serial.println("❌ Access Denied!");
      blinkLED(RED_LED_PIN);
    }
    cardPresent = true;
  }

  rfid.PICC_HaltA();
  rfid.PCD_StopCrypto1();
}

bool isAuthorizedCard(byte *uid, byte size) {
  for (int i = 0; i < totalAuthorizedCards; i++) {
    bool match = true;
    for (int j = 0; j < size; j++) {
      if (uid[j] != authorizedUIDs[i][j]) {
        match = false;
        break;
      }
    }
    if (match) return true;
  }
  return false;
}

void blinkLED(int pin) {
  digitalWrite(pin, HIGH);
  delay(500);
  digitalWrite(pin, LOW);
}
